      <p><b>Georgia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>: <span lang="ka" title="Georgian-language text">საქართველო</span>, <span style="font-size: smaller;"><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Georgian" title="Romanization of Georgian">romanized</a>:</span> <span lang="ka-Latn" style="font-style: italic;">sakartvelo</span>; <small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Georgian" title="Help:IPA/Georgian">[sɑkʰɑrtʰvɛlɔ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sakartvelo.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Sakartvelo.ogg" class="internal" title="Sakartvelo.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> region, at the <a href="/wiki/Europe%E2%80%93Asia_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Europe–Asia border">the intersection</a> of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. It is bounded to the west by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, to the north and east by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, to the south by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, and to the southeast by <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Georgia_(country)" title="List of cities and towns in Georgia (country)">largest city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>. Georgia covers a territory of 69,700 square kilometres (26,911&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and its approximate population is about 3.718&nbsp;million. Georgia is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary">parliamentary republic</a>, with the government elected through a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>. </p>
      <p>Georgia is <a href="/wiki/History_of_wine" title="History of wine">one of the oldest wine-producing countries</a> in the world; local traditions associated with <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> are entwined with Georgia's national identity<sup id="cite_ref-Vinologue_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vinologue-11">[11]</a></sup> and have been classified by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as part of the world's Intangible Cultural Heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical era</a>, several independent kingdoms became established in what is now Georgia, such as <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">Colchis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iberia_(antiquity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Iberia (antiquity)">Iberia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a> officially <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Iberia" title="Christianization of Iberia">adopted Christianity</a> in the early 4th century. The <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian Orthodox Church</a> contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">spiritual</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia#Unification_of_the_Georgian_State" title="Kingdom of Georgia">political unification</a> of early <a href="/wiki/List_of_historical_states_of_Georgia#Early_Middle_Ages" title="List of historical states of Georgia">Georgian states</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the unified <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Kingdom of Georgia</a> emerged and reached its <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Golden_Age" title="Georgian Golden Age">Golden Age</a> during the reign of King <a href="/wiki/David_IV_of_Georgia" title="David IV of Georgia">David the Builder</a> and Queen <a href="/wiki/Tamar_of_Georgia" title="Tamar of Georgia">Tamar the Great</a> in the 12th and early 13th centuries. Thereafter, the kingdom declined and eventually <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia#Final_disintegration" title="Kingdom of Georgia">disintegrated</a> under the hegemony of various regional powers, including the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and successive dynasties of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Persia</a>. In 1783, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli-Kakheti" title="Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti">one of the Georgian kingdoms</a> entered <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Georgievsk" title="Treaty of Georgievsk">an alliance</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, which proceeded to <a href="/wiki/Georgia_within_the_Russian_Empire" title="Georgia within the Russian Empire">annex</a> the territory of modern Georgia in a piecemeal fashion throughout the 19th century. </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> in 1917, Georgia emerged as an independent <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">republic</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> under <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Poti" title="Treaty of Poti">German protection</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German</a> defeat in <a href="/wiki/WWI" class="mw-redirect" title="WWI">WWI</a>, Georgia was <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Georgia" title="Red Army invasion of Georgia">invaded by Bolshevik Russia</a>, resulting in the country's eventual incorporation into the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in 1922. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, almost 700,000 Georgians fought in the Red Army against the Germans. By the 1980s, an independence movement was established and grew, leading to Georgia's secession from the Soviet Union in April 1991. For most of the subsequent decade, <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-Soviet">post-Soviet</a> Georgia suffered from economic crisis, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Civil_War" title="Georgian Civil War">civil</a> and secessionist wars in <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>. Following the bloodless <a href="/wiki/Rose_Revolution" title="Rose Revolution">Rose Revolution</a> in 2003, Georgia strongly pursued a pro-Western foreign policy; it introduced a series of democratic and economic reforms aimed at <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">NATO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">European integration</a>. The country's Western orientation soon led to the worsening of <a href="/wiki/Georgia%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="Georgia–Russia relations">relations with Russia</a>, at one point even resulting in <a href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War" title="Russo-Georgian War">a brief war</a>. </p>
      <p>Georgia is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> classified as "very high" on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. The country is a member of international organizations across both Europe and Asia, such as <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurocontrol" title="Eurocontrol">Eurocontrol</a>, <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a> and the <a href="/wiki/GUAM_Organization_for_Democracy_and_Economic_Development" title="GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development">GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Etymology"></span> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Georgia_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of Georgia (country)">Names of Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg/220px-Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg/330px-Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg/440px-Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="616" data-file-height="282"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gorgania_on_Fra_Mauro_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>"Gorgania" i.e. Georgia on <a href="/wiki/Fra_Mauro_map" title="Fra Mauro map">Fra Mauro map</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first mention of the name <a href="/wiki/Spelling" title="Spelling">spelled</a> as “Georgia” is in <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Mappa_mundi" title="Mappa mundi">mappa mundi</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Vesconte" title="Pietro Vesconte">Pietro Vesconte</a> dated AD 1320,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> At the early stage of its appearance in the Latin world, it was not always written in the same transliteration, and the first consonant was being spelt with <i>J</i> as "Jorgia".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> "Georgia" probably stems from the <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Persian</a> designation of the Georgians – <i>gurğān</i>, in the 11th and 12th centuries adapted via <a href="/wiki/Syriac_language" title="Syriac language">Syriac</a> <i>gurz-ān</i>/<i>gurz-iyān</i> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> <i>ĵurĵan</i>/<i>ĵurzan</i>. Lore-based theories were given by the traveller <a href="/wiki/Jacques_de_Vitry" title="Jacques de Vitry">Jacques de Vitry</a>, who explained the name's origin by the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">St. George</a> amongst Georgians,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> while traveller <a href="/wiki/Jean_Chardin" title="Jean Chardin">Jean Chardin</a> thought that "Georgia" came from Greek γεωργός ("tiller of the land"). As Prof. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Mikaberidze" title="Alexander Mikaberidze">Alexander Mikaberidze</a> adds, these century-old explanations for the word <i>Georgia/Georgians</i> are rejected by the scholarly community, who point to the <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> word <i>gurğ/gurğān</i> ("wolf"<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>) as the root of the word.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia-18">[18]</a></sup> Starting with the Persian word <i>gurğ/gurğān</i>, the word was later adopted in numerous other languages, including Slavic and West European languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This term itself might have been established through the ancient Iranian appellation of the near-<a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> region, which was referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Hyrcania" title="Hyrcania">Gorgan</a></i> ("land of the wolves").<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The native name is <i>Sakartvelo</i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%83%A1%E1%83%90%E1%83%A5%E1%83%90%E1%83%A0%E1%83%97%E1%83%95%E1%83%94%E1%83%9A%E1%83%9D" class="extiw" title="wikt:საქართველო">საქართველო</a>; "land of <a href="/wiki/Kartvelian_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Kartvelian peoples">Kartvelians</a>"), derived from the core central Georgian region of <a href="/wiki/Kartli" title="Kartli">Kartli</a>, recorded from the 9th century, and in extended usage referring to the entire medieval <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Kingdom of Georgia</a> by the 13th century. The self-designation used by <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">ethnic Georgians</a> is <i>Kartvelebi</i> (ქართველები, i.e. "<a href="/wiki/Kartvelian_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Kartvelian peoples">Kartvelians</a>"). </p>
      <p>The medieval <a href="/wiki/The_Georgian_Chronicles" title="The Georgian Chronicles">Georgian Chronicles</a> present an eponymous ancestor of the Kartvelians, <a href="/wiki/Kartlos" title="Kartlos">Kartlos</a>, a great-grandson of <a href="/wiki/Japheth" title="Japheth">Japheth</a>. However, scholars agree that the word is derived from the <i>Karts</i>, the latter being one of the proto-Georgian tribes that emerged as a dominant group in ancient times.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Dictionary_of_Georgia-18">[18]</a></sup> The name <i>Sakartvelo</i> (საქართველო) consists of two parts. Its root, <i>kartvel-i</i> (ქართველ-ი), specifies an inhabitant of the core central-eastern Georgian region of <a href="/wiki/Kartli" title="Kartli">Kartli</a>, or Iberia as it is known in sources of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greeks" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greeks">Ancient Greeks</a> (<a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a>, etc.) and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> (<a href="/wiki/Titus_Livius" class="mw-redirect" title="Titus Livius">Titus Livius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a>, etc.) referred to early western Georgians as <a href="/wiki/Colchians" class="mw-redirect" title="Colchians">Colchians</a> and eastern Georgians as <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Iberians" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasian Iberians">Iberians</a> (<i>Iberoi</i> in some Greek sources).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Georgian <a href="/wiki/Circumfix" title="Circumfix">circumfix</a> <i>sa</i>-X-<i>o</i> is a standard geographic construction designating "the area where X dwell", where X is an <a href="/wiki/Ethnonym" title="Ethnonym">ethnonym</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rapp_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rapp-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today the full, official name of the country is "Georgia", as specified in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Constitution of Georgia (country)">Georgian constitution</a> which reads "<i>Georgia</i> is the name of the state of Georgia."<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Before the 1995 constitution came into force the country's name was the <i>Republic of Georgia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[a]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Georgia_(country)" title="History of Georgia (country)">History of Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Georgia" title="Prehistoric Georgia">Prehistoric Georgia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_(Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum)_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_%28Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum%29_3.jpg/220px-State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_%28Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum%29_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_%28Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum%29_3.jpg/330px-State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_%28Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum%29_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_%28Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum%29_3.jpg/440px-State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_%28Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum%29_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1875"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:State_Museum_of_History_of_Georgia_(Tbilisi_Archaeological_Museum)_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Patera" title="Patera">Patera</a> depicting <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">Marcus Aurelius</a> uncovered in central Georgia, 2nd century AD
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Georgian_National_Museum_15043_(9067066727).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Georgian_National_Museum_15043_%289067066727%29.jpg/220px-Georgian_National_Museum_15043_%289067066727%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Georgian_National_Museum_15043_%289067066727%29.jpg/330px-Georgian_National_Museum_15043_%289067066727%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Georgian_National_Museum_15043_%289067066727%29.jpg/440px-Georgian_National_Museum_15043_%289067066727%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Georgian_National_Museum_15043_(9067066727).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ceremonial bowl of <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sassanian</a> origin, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_National_Museum" title="Georgian National Museum">Georgian National Museum</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The territory of modern-day Georgia was inhabited by <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> since the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic Era</a>. The proto-Georgian tribes first appear in written history in the 12th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-PhoenixThe_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhoenixThe-26">[25]</a></sup> The earliest evidence of <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> to date has been found in Georgia, where 8,000-year old wine jars were uncovered.<sup id="cite_ref-independent8k_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent8k-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Archaeological finds and references in ancient sources also reveal elements of early political and state formations characterized by advanced <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a> and goldsmith techniques that date back to the 7th century BC and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-PhoenixThe_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhoenixThe-26">[25]</a></sup> In fact, early metallurgy started in Georgia during the 6th millennium BC, associated with the <a href="/wiki/Shulaveri-Shomu_culture" title="Shulaveri-Shomu culture">Shulaveri-Shomu culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-saunje.ge_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saunje.ge-29">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical period</a> saw the rise of a number of early Georgian states, the principal of which were <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">Colchis</a> in the west and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iberia_(antiquity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Iberia (antiquity)">Iberia</a> in the east. In <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythology</a>, Colchis was the location of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Fleece" title="Golden Fleece">Golden Fleece</a> sought by <a href="/wiki/Jason" title="Jason">Jason</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Argonauts" title="Argonauts">Argonauts</a> in <a href="/wiki/Apollonius_of_Rhodes" title="Apollonius of Rhodes">Apollonius Rhodius</a>' epic tale <i><a href="/wiki/Argonautica" title="Argonautica">Argonautica</a></i>. The incorporation of the Golden Fleece into the myth may have derived from the local practice of using fleeces to sift gold dust from rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-LOCge15_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOCge15-30">[29]</a></sup> In the 4th century BC, a kingdom of Iberia – an early example of advanced state organization under one king and an aristocratic hierarchy – was established.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> completed its <a href="/wiki/Pompey%27s_Georgian_campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Pompey's Georgian campaign">brief conquest</a> of what is now Georgia in 66 BC, the area became a primary objective of what would eventually turn out to be <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars" title="Roman–Persian Wars">over 700 years</a> of protracted <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Iranian_relations" title="Roman–Iranian relations">Irano–Roman</a> geo-political rivalry and warfare.<sup id="cite_ref-Armenia,_Azerbaijan_1996,_p._158_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armenia,_Azerbaijan_1996,_p._158-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> From the first centuries A.D, the cult of <a href="/wiki/Mithraism" title="Mithraism">Mithras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> beliefs, and <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a> were commonly practised in Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> In 337 AD King <a href="/wiki/Mirian_III_of_Iberia" title="Mirian III of Iberia">Mirian III</a> declared Christianity as the <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Iberia" title="Christianization of Iberia">state religion</a>, giving a great stimulus to the development of literature, arts, and ultimately playing a key role in the formation of the unified Georgian nation,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> The acceptance led to the slow but sure decline of Zoroastrianism,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> which until the 5th century AD, appeared to have become something like a second established religion in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iberia_(antiquity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Iberia (antiquity)">Iberia</a> (eastern Georgia), and was widely practised there.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_up_to_early_modern_period">Middle Ages up to early modern period</span></h3> 
      <p>Located on the crossroads of protracted <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars" title="Roman–Persian Wars">Roman–Persian wars</a>, the early Georgian kingdoms disintegrated into various feudal regions by the early <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. This made it easy for the remaining Georgian realms to fall prey to the <a href="/wiki/Arab_rule_in_Georgia" title="Arab rule in Georgia">early Muslim conquests</a> in the 7th century. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bagratid_Iberia">Bagratid Iberia</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_(Photo_A._Muhranoff,_2011).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_%28Photo_A._Muhranoff%2C_2011%29.jpg/220px-Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_%28Photo_A._Muhranoff%2C_2011%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_%28Photo_A._Muhranoff%2C_2011%29.jpg/330px-Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_%28Photo_A._Muhranoff%2C_2011%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_%28Photo_A._Muhranoff%2C_2011%29.jpg/440px-Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_%28Photo_A._Muhranoff%2C_2011%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1196" data-file-height="998"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mulakhi_community._Svan_towers_(Photo_A._Muhranoff,_2011).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Northwestern Georgia is home to <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval</a> defensive <a href="/wiki/Tower_house" title="Tower house">tower houses</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ushguli" title="Ushguli">Ushguli</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The extinction of the Iberian royal dynasties, such as <a href="/wiki/Guaramid_dynasty" title="Guaramid dynasty">Guaramids</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chosroid_dynasty" title="Chosroid dynasty">Chosroids</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> and also the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid</a> preoccupation with their own civil wars and conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, led to the <a href="/wiki/Bagrationi_dynasty" title="Bagrationi dynasty">Bagrationi</a> family's growth in prominence. The head of the Bagrationi dynasty <a href="/wiki/Ashot_I_of_Iberia" title="Ashot I of Iberia">Ashot I of Iberia</a> (r.813–826), who had migrated to the former southwestern territories of Iberia, came to rule over <a href="/wiki/Tao-Klarjeti_(historical_region)" title="Tao-Klarjeti (historical region)">Tao-Klarjeti</a> and restored the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Tao-Klarjeti" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Tao-Klarjeti">Principate of Iberia</a> in 813. The sons and grandsons of Ashot I established three separate branches, frequently struggling with each other and with neighboring rulers. The Kartli line prevailed; in 888 <a href="/wiki/Adarnase_IV_of_Iberia" title="Adarnase IV of Iberia">Adarnase IV of Iberia</a> (r.888–923) restored the indigenous royal authority dormant since 580. Despite the revitalization of the <a href="/wiki/Bagratid_Iberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagratid Iberia">Iberian monarchy</a>, remaining Georgian lands were divided among rival authorities, with Tbilisi remaining in <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Tbilisi" title="Emirate of Tbilisi">Arab hands</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Abkhazia">Kingdom of Abkhazia</span></h4> 
      <p>An <a href="/wiki/Marwan_ibn_Muhammad%27s_invasion_of_Georgia" title="Marwan ibn Muhammad's invasion of Georgia">Arab incursion</a> into western Georgia led by <a href="/wiki/Marwan_II" title="Marwan II">Marwan II</a>, was repelled by <a href="/wiki/Leon_I_of_Abkhazia" title="Leon I of Abkhazia">Leon I</a> (r.720–740) jointly with his Lazic and <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Iberia" title="Principality of Iberia">Iberian</a> allies in 736. Leon I then married <a href="/wiki/Mirian_of_Kakheti" title="Mirian of Kakheti">Mirian</a>'s daughter, and a successor, <a href="/wiki/Leon_II_of_Abkhazia" title="Leon II of Abkhazia">Leon II</a> exploited this dynastic union to acquire <a href="/wiki/Lazica" title="Lazica">Lazica</a> in the 770s.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> The successful defense against the Arabs, and new territorial gains, gave the Abkhazian princes enough power to claim more autonomy from the Byzantine Empire. Towards circa 778, <a href="/wiki/Leon_II_of_Abkhazia" title="Leon II of Abkhazia">Leon II</a> (r.780–828) won his full independence with the help of the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a> and was crowned as the <a href="/wiki/Divan_of_the_Abkhazian_Kings" title="Divan of the Abkhazian Kings">king of Abkhazia</a>. After obtaining independence for the state, the matter of church independence became the main problem. In the early 9th century the Abkhazian Church broke away from the <a href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriarchate of Constantinople">Constantinople</a> and recognized the authority of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_the_Georgian_Orthodox_Church#Catholicoi_of_Kartli_(467–1010)" title="List of heads of the Georgian Orthodox Church">Catholicate of Mtskheta</a>; Georgian language replaced <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> as the language of literacy and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> The most prosperous period of the Abkhazian kingdom was between 850 and 950. A bitter <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">civil war</a> and feudal revolts which began under <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_III_of_Abkhazia" title="Demetrius III of Abkhazia">Demetrius III</a> (r. 967–975) led the kingdom into complete anarchy under the unfortunate king <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_III_of_Abkhazia" title="Theodosius III of Abkhazia">Theodosius III the Blind</a> (r. 975–978). A period of unrest ensued, which ended as Abkhazia and eastern Georgian states were <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia#Unification_of_the_Georgian_State" title="Kingdom of Georgia">unified</a> under a single <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Georgian monarchy</a>, ruled by King <a href="/wiki/Bagrat_III_of_Georgia" title="Bagrat III of Georgia">Bagrat III of Georgia</a> (r. 975–1014), due largely to the diplomacy and conquests of his energetic foster-father <a href="/wiki/David_III_of_Tao" title="David III of Tao">David III of Tao</a> (r. 966–1001). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg/220px-Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg/330px-Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg/440px-Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gelati_Monastery_2013-7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Gelati_Monastery" title="Gelati Monastery">Gelati Monastery</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage Site, was built in the 12th century by King David IV
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Georgian_monarchy">United Georgian monarchy</span></h4> 
      <p>The stage of <a href="/wiki/Georgian_feudalism" title="Georgian feudalism">feudalism</a>'s development and struggle against common invaders as much as <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">common belief</a> of various Georgian states had an enormous importance for spiritual and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia#Unification_of_the_Georgian_State" title="Kingdom of Georgia">political unification</a> of Georgia feudal monarchy under the <a href="/wiki/Bagrationi_dynasty" title="Bagrationi dynasty">Bagrationi dynasty</a> in 11th century. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Kingdom of Georgia</a> reached its zenith in the 12th to early 13th centuries. This period during the reigns of <a href="/wiki/David_IV_of_Georgia" title="David IV of Georgia">David IV</a> (r.1089–1125) and his granddaughter <a href="/wiki/Tamar_of_Georgia" title="Tamar of Georgia">Tamar</a> (r.1184–1213) has been widely termed as <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Golden_Age" title="Georgian Golden Age">Georgia's Golden Age</a> or the Georgian Renaissance.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> This early Georgian renaissance, which preceded its Western European analogue, was characterized by impressive military victories, territorial expansion, and a cultural renaissance in architecture, literature, philosophy and the sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> The Golden age of Georgia left a legacy of great cathedrals, romantic poetry and literature, and the epic poem <i><a href="/wiki/The_Knight_in_the_Panther%27s_Skin" title="The Knight in the Panther's Skin">The Knight in the Panther's Skin</a></i>, the latter which is considered a <a href="/wiki/National_epic" title="National epic">national epic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tamar_(Vardzia_fresco_detail).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Tamar_%28Vardzia_fresco_detail%29.jpg/170px-Tamar_%28Vardzia_fresco_detail%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Tamar_%28Vardzia_fresco_detail%29.jpg/255px-Tamar_%28Vardzia_fresco_detail%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Tamar_%28Vardzia_fresco_detail%29.jpg/340px-Tamar_%28Vardzia_fresco_detail%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="759"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tamar_(Vardzia_fresco_detail).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tamar_of_Georgia" title="Tamar of Georgia">Queen Tamara</a>, the first woman to rule Georgia in her own right and regarded as "King of Kings".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEastmond109_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastmond109-47">[46]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>David suppressed dissent of feudal lords and centralized the power in his hands to effectively deal with foreign threats. In 1121, he decisively defeated much larger Turkish armies during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Didgori" title="Battle of Didgori">Battle of Didgori</a> and liberated Tbilisi.<sup id="cite_ref-javaxisvili_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-javaxisvili-48">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 29-year reign of Tamar, the first female ruler of Georgia, is considered the most successful in Georgian history.<sup id="cite_ref-Eastmond_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eastmond-49">[48]</a></sup> Tamar was given the title "king of kings" (<i><a href="/wiki/Mepe_(title)" title="Mepe (title)">mepe</a> mepeta</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEastmond109_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastmond109-47">[46]</a></sup> She succeeded in neutralizing opposition and embarked on an energetic foreign policy aided by the downfall of the rival powers of the Seljuks and Byzantium. Supported by a powerful military élite, Tamar was able to build on the successes of her predecessors to consolidate an empire which dominated the Caucasus, and extended over large parts of present-day Azerbaijan, Armenia, and eastern Turkey as well as parts of northern Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> until its collapse under the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Georgia" title="Mongol invasions of Georgia">Mongol attacks</a> within two decades after Tamar's death in 1213.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEastmond93-95_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEastmond93-95-51">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The revival of the Kingdom of Georgia was set back after Tbilisi was captured and destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">Khwarezmian</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Jalal_ad-Din_Mingburnu" title="Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu">Jalal ad-Din</a> in 1226.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> The Mongols were expelled by <a href="/wiki/George_V_of_Georgia" title="George V of Georgia">George V of Georgia</a> (r.1299–1302), son of <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_II_of_Georgia" title="Demetrius II of Georgia">Demetrius II of Georgia</a> (r.1270–1289), who was named "Brilliant" for his role in restoring the country's previous strength and Christian culture. George V was the last great king of the unified Georgian state. After his death, local rulers fought for their independence from central Georgian rule, until the total disintegration of the Kingdom in the 15th century. Georgia was further weakened by several <a href="/wiki/Timur%27s_invasions_of_Georgia" title="Timur's invasions of Georgia">disastrous invasions</a> by <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Tamerlane</a>. <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_incursions_into_Georgia" title="Turkmen incursions into Georgia">Invasions continued</a>, giving the kingdom no time for restoration, with both <a href="/wiki/Kara_Koyunlu" title="Kara Koyunlu">Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aq_Qoyunlu" title="Aq Qoyunlu">White</a> sheep Turkomans constantly raiding its southern provinces. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tripartite_division">Tripartite division</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pizigani_1367_Chart_(Cropped_Tbilisi).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Pizigani_1367_Chart_%28Cropped_Tbilisi%29.jpg/220px-Pizigani_1367_Chart_%28Cropped_Tbilisi%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Pizigani_1367_Chart_%28Cropped_Tbilisi%29.jpg/330px-Pizigani_1367_Chart_%28Cropped_Tbilisi%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Pizigani_1367_Chart_%28Cropped_Tbilisi%29.jpg/440px-Pizigani_1367_Chart_%28Cropped_Tbilisi%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="858"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pizigani_1367_Chart_(Cropped_Tbilisi).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Detail from a 14th-century map by <a href="/wiki/Domenico_and_Francesco_Pizzigano" title="Domenico and Francesco Pizzigano">Domenico and Francesco Pizzigano</a>, showing historical <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Flag of Georgia (country)">Flag of Georgia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Kingdom of Georgia <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia#Final_disintegration" title="Kingdom of Georgia">collapsed</a> into anarchy by 1466 and fragmented into three independent kingdoms and five semi-independent principalities. Neighboring large empires subsequently exploited the internal division of the weakened country, and beginning in the 16th century up to the late 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid Iran</a> (and successive Iranian <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">Afsharid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar</a> dynasties) and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkey">Ottoman Turkey</a> subjugated the eastern and western regions of Georgia, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The rulers of regions that remained partly <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomous</a> organized rebellions on various occasions. However, subsequent Iranian and Ottoman invasions further weakened local kingdoms and regions. As a result of incessant <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars" title="Ottoman–Persian Wars">Ottoman–Persian Wars</a> and deportations, the population of Georgia dwindled to 784,700 inhabitants at the end of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Georgia_(country)" title="Eastern Georgia (country)">Eastern Georgia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Safavid_Georgia" title="Safavid Georgia">Safavid Georgia</a>), composed of the regions of <a href="/wiki/Kartli" title="Kartli">Kartli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kakheti" title="Kakheti">Kakheti</a>, had been under Iranian <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> since 1555 following the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amasya" title="Peace of Amasya">Peace of Amasya</a> signed with neighbouring rivalling Ottoman Turkey. With the death of <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nader Shah</a> in 1747, both kingdoms broke free of Iranian control and were reunified through <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli-Kakheti" title="Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti">a personal union</a> under the energetic king <a href="/wiki/Heraclius_II_of_Georgia" title="Heraclius II of Georgia">Heraclius II</a> in 1762. Heraclius, who had risen to prominence through the Iranian ranks, was awarded the crown of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli" title="Kingdom of Kartli">Kartli</a> by Nader himself in 1744 for his loyal service to him.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Heraclius nevertheless stabilized Eastern Georgia to a degree in the ensuing period and was able to guarantee its autonomy throughout the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Zand_dynasty" title="Zand dynasty">Zand</a> period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFisherAveryHamblyMelville1991328_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFisherAveryHamblyMelville1991328-56">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1783, Russia and the eastern Georgian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli-Kakheti" title="Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti">Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Georgievsk" title="Treaty of Georgievsk">Treaty of Georgievsk</a>, by which Georgia abjured any dependence on <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persia</a> or another power, and made the kingdom a protectorate of Russia, which guaranteed Georgia's territorial integrity and the continuation of its reigning Bagrationi dynasty in return for prerogatives in the conduct of Georgian foreign affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg/170px-George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg/255px-George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg/340px-George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="520"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:George_XII_of_Georgia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>King <a href="/wiki/George_XII_of_Georgia" title="George XII of Georgia">George XII</a> was the last king of <a href="/wiki/Kartli_and_Kakheti" class="mw-redirect" title="Kartli and Kakheti">Kartli and Kakheti</a>, which was annexed by Russia in 1801.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>However, despite this commitment to defend Georgia, Russia rendered no assistance when the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Iranians</a> invaded in 1795, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krtsanisi" title="Battle of Krtsanisi">capturing and sacking Tbilisi</a> while massacring its inhabitants, as the new heir to the throne sought to reassert Iranian hegemony over Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Despite a <a href="/wiki/Persian_Expedition_of_1796" title="Persian Expedition of 1796">punitive campaign</a> subsequently launched against Qajar Iran in 1796, this period culminated in the 1801 Russian violation of the Treaty of Georgievsk and annexation of eastern Georgia, followed by the abolition of the royal <a href="/wiki/Bagrationi_dynasty" title="Bagrationi dynasty">Bagrationi dynasty</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Autocephaly" title="Autocephaly">autocephaly</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian Orthodox Church</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Bagration" title="Pyotr Bagration">Pyotr Bagration</a>, one of the descendants of the abolished house of Bagrationi, would later join the Russian army and rise to be a prominent general in the Napoleonic wars.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia_in_the_Russian_Empire">Georgia in the Russian Empire</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Georgia_within_the_Russian_Empire" title="Georgia within the Russian Empire">Georgia within the Russian Empire</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_(1765-1812)_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_%281765-1812%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_%281765-1812%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_%281765-1812%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_%281765-1812%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_%281765-1812%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_%281765-1812%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3420" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:George_Dawe_-_Portrait_of_General_Pyotr_Bagration_(1765-1812)_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Bagration" title="Pyotr Bagration">Pyotr Bagration</a>, Georgian prince of the royal <a href="/wiki/Bagrationi_dynasty" title="Bagrationi dynasty">Bagrationi dynasty</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 22 December 1800, <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsar</a> <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Paul I of Russia</a>, at the alleged request of the Georgian King <a href="/wiki/Giorgi_XII_of_Kartli-Kakheti" class="mw-redirect" title="Giorgi XII of Kartli-Kakheti">George XII</a>, signed the proclamation on the incorporation of Georgia (Kartli-Kakheti) within the Russian Empire, which was finalized by a decree on 8 January 1801,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> and confirmed by Tsar <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I</a> on 12 September 1801.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bagrationi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagrationi">Bagrationi</a> royal family was deported from the kingdom. The Georgian envoy in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> reacted with a note of protest that was presented to the Russian vice-chancellor Prince Kurakin.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> In May 1801, under the oversight of General Carl Heinrich von Knorring, Imperial Russia transferred power in eastern Georgia to the government headed by General <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Petrovich_Lazarev&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ivan Petrovich Lazarev (page does not exist)">Ivan Petrovich Lazarev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> The Georgian nobility did not accept the decree until 12 April 1802, when Knorring assembled the nobility at the <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi_Sioni_Cathedral" title="Tbilisi Sioni Cathedral">Sioni Cathedral</a> and forced them to take an oath on the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Crown_of_Russia" title="Imperial Crown of Russia">Imperial Crown of Russia</a>. Those who disagreed were temporarily arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the summer of 1805, Russian troops on the Askerani River near <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zagam,_Georgia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zagam, Georgia (page does not exist)">Zagam</a> defeated the Iranian army during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">1804–13 Russo-Persian War</a> and saved Tbilisi from reconquest now that it was officially part of the Imperial territories. Russian suzerainty over eastern Georgia was officially finalized with Iran in 1813 following the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Treaty of Gulistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Following the annexation of eastern Georgia, the western Georgian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Imereti" title="Kingdom of Imereti">kingdom of Imereti</a> was annexed by Tsar Alexander I. The last Imeretian king and the last Georgian Bagrationi ruler, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_II_of_Imereti" title="Solomon II of Imereti">Solomon II</a>, died in exile in 1815, after attempts to rally people against Russia and to enlist foreign support against the latter, had been in vain.<sup id="cite_ref-Suny_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suny-68">[67]</a></sup> From 1803 to 1878, as a result of numerous Russian wars now against <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkey">Ottoman Turkey</a>, several of Georgia's previously lost territories – such as <a href="/wiki/Adjara" title="Adjara">Adjara</a> – were recovered, and also incorporated into the empire. The principality of <a href="/wiki/Guria" title="Guria">Guria</a> was abolished and incorporated into the Empire in 1829, while <a href="/wiki/Svaneti" title="Svaneti">Svaneti</a> was gradually annexed in 1858. <a href="/wiki/Samegrelo" class="mw-redirect" title="Samegrelo">Mingrelia</a>, although a Russian protectorate since 1803, was not absorbed until 1867.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Declaration_of_independence">Declaration of independence</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">Democratic Republic of Georgia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Noe_Schordania.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Noe_Schordania.jpg/170px-Noe_Schordania.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Noe_Schordania.jpg/255px-Noe_Schordania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Noe_Schordania.jpg/340px-Noe_Schordania.jpg 2x" data-file-width="563" data-file-height="692"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Noe_Schordania.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Noe_Zhordania" title="Noe Zhordania">Noe Zhordania</a>, Prime Minister of Georgia who was exiled to <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> after the Soviet takeover
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of 1917, the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Democratic_Federative_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic">Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic</a> was established with <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Chkheidze" title="Nikolay Chkheidze">Nikolay Chkheidze</a> acting as its president. The federation consisted of three nations: Georgia, Armenia and Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> As the Ottomans advanced into the Caucasian territories of the crumbling Russian Empire, Georgia declared independence on 26 May 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-71">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Menshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Menshevik">Menshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Georgia" title="Social Democratic Party of Georgia">Social Democratic Party of Georgia</a> won the parliamentary election and its leader, <a href="/wiki/Noe_Zhordania" title="Noe Zhordania">Noe Zhordania</a>, became prime minister. Despite the Soviet takeover, Zhordania was recognized as the legitimate head of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia_in_Exile" title="Government of the Democratic Republic of Georgia in Exile">Georgian Government</a> by France, UK, Belgium, and Poland through the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1918 <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Armenian_War" title="Georgian–Armenian War">Georgian–Armenian War</a>, which erupted over parts of disputed provinces between Armenia and Georgia populated mostly by Armenians, ended because of British intervention. In 1918–1919, Georgian general <a href="/wiki/Giorgi_Mazniashvili" title="Giorgi Mazniashvili">Giorgi Mazniashvili</a> led an attack against the <a href="/wiki/White_Army" title="White Army">White Army</a> led by Moiseev and Denikin in order to claim the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coastline from <a href="/wiki/Tuapse" title="Tuapse">Tuapse</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adlersky_City_District" title="Adlersky City District">Adler</a> for the independent Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-shirokov_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shirokov-73">[72]</a></sup> The country's independence did not last long, being annexed by the Soviet Union in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-71">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia_in_the_Soviet_Union">Georgia in the Soviet Union</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian Affair">Georgian Affair</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg/220px-Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg/330px-Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg/440px-Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg 2x" data-file-width="579" data-file-height="410"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Red_Army_in_Tbilisi_Feb_25_1921.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 11th Red Army of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a> holds a military parade, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Occupation_Day,_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Occupation Day, Georgia">25 February 1921</a> in Tbilisi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ordzhonikidze,_Stalin_and_Mikoyan,_1925.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ordzhonikidze%2C_Stalin_and_Mikoyan%2C_1925.jpg/220px-Ordzhonikidze%2C_Stalin_and_Mikoyan%2C_1925.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ordzhonikidze%2C_Stalin_and_Mikoyan%2C_1925.jpg/330px-Ordzhonikidze%2C_Stalin_and_Mikoyan%2C_1925.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Ordzhonikidze%2C_Stalin_and_Mikoyan%2C_1925.jpg/440px-Ordzhonikidze%2C_Stalin_and_Mikoyan%2C_1925.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1060"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ordzhonikidze,_Stalin_and_Mikoyan,_1925.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Anastas_Mikoyan" title="Anastas Mikoyan">Anastas Mikoyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergo_Ordzhonikidze" title="Sergo Ordzhonikidze">Sergo Ordzhonikidze</a> in Tbilisi, 1925
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In February 1921, during the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Georgia" title="Red Army invasion of Georgia">Red Army advanced into Georgia</a> and brought the local Bolsheviks to power. The Georgian army was defeated and the Social Democratic government fled the country. On <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Occupation_Day,_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Occupation Day, Georgia">25 February 1921</a>, the Red Army entered Tbilisi and established a government of workers' and peasants' <a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">soviets</a> with <a href="/wiki/Filipp_Makharadze" title="Filipp Makharadze">Filipp Makharadze</a> as acting head of state. Georgia was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Socialist_Federative_Soviet_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic">Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijan</a>, in 1921 which in 1922 would become a founding member of the Soviet Union. </p>
      <p>There remained significant opposition to the Bolsheviks in Georgia, which was unindustrialized and viewed as socially backward, and this culminated in the <a href="/wiki/August_Uprising" title="August Uprising">August Uprising</a> of 1924. Soviet rule was firmly established only after the insurrection was swiftly defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Georgia would remain an unindustrialized periphery of the USSR until the <a href="/wiki/First_five-year_plan" title="First five-year plan">first five-year plan</a> when it would become a major center for textile goods. Later, in 1936, the TSFSR was dissolved and Georgia emerged as a <a href="/wiki/Union_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Union republic">union republic</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, an ethnic Georgian born Iosif Vissarionovich Jugashvili (იოსებ ბესარიონის ძე ჯუღაშვილი) in <a href="/wiki/Gori,_Georgia" title="Gori, Georgia">Gori</a>, was prominent among the Bolsheviks.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Stalin was to rise to the highest position, leading the Soviet Union from the mid–1920s until his death on 5 March 1953. </p>
      <p>In June 1941, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarosa" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Barbarosa">invaded the Soviet Union</a> on an immediate course towards Caucasian oil fields and munitions factories. They never reached Georgia, however, and almost 700,000 Georgians fought in the Red Army to repel the invaders and advance towards Berlin. Of them, an estimated 350,000 were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Georgian_uprising_on_Texel" title="Georgian uprising on Texel">Georgian uprising on Texel</a> against the Germans was the last battle of the World War II in Europe. </p>
      <p>After Stalin's death, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> became the leader of the Soviet Union and implemented a policy of <a href="/wiki/De-Stalinization" title="De-Stalinization">de-Stalinization</a>. This was nowhere else more publicly and violently opposed than in Georgia, where in 1956 riots broke out upon the release of Khruschev's <a href="/wiki/On_the_Cult_of_Personality_and_Its_Consequences" title="On the Cult of Personality and Its Consequences">public denunciation of Stalin</a> and led to the death of nearly 100 students. </p>
      <p>Throughout the remainder of the Soviet period, Georgia's economy continued to grow and experience significant improvement, though it increasingly exhibited blatant corruption and alienation of the government from the people. With the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a> in 1986, the Georgian Communist leadership proved so incapable of handling the changes that most Georgians, including <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/rank_and_file" class="extiw" title="wikt:Special:Search/rank and file">rank and file</a> Communists, concluded that the only way forward was a break from the existing Soviet system. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgia_after_restoration_of_independence">Georgia after restoration of independence</span></h3> 
      <p>On 9 April 1991, shortly before the collapse of the Soviet Union, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_the_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Supreme Council of the Republic of Georgia">Supreme Council</a> of Georgia declared independence after a <a href="/wiki/Georgian_independence_referendum,_1991" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian independence referendum, 1991">referendum</a> held on 31 March 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-GovtofGeorgia_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovtofGeorgia-77">[76]</a></sup> On 26 May 1991, <a href="/wiki/Zviad_Gamsakhurdia" title="Zviad Gamsakhurdia">Zviad Gamsakhurdia</a> was elected as the first President of independent Georgia. Gamsakhurdia stoked Georgian nationalism and vowed to assert Tbilisi's authority over regions such as Abkhazia and South Ossetia that had been classified as autonomous <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblasts</a> under the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton-78">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1993_Georgia_war1.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/1993_Georgia_war1.svg/220px-1993_Georgia_war1.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/1993_Georgia_war1.svg/330px-1993_Georgia_war1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/1993_Georgia_war1.svg/440px-1993_Georgia_war1.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1940" data-file-height="1370"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1993_Georgia_war1.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Georgian_Civil_War" title="Georgian Civil War">Georgian Civil War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%931993)" title="War in Abkhazia (1992–1993)">War in Abkhazia</a> in August–October 1993
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>He was soon deposed in a <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Georgian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1991–92 Georgian coup d'état">bloody <i>coup d'état</i></a>, from 22 December 1991 to 6 January 1992. The coup was instigated by part of the National Guards and a paramilitary organization called "<a href="/wiki/Mkhedrioni" title="Mkhedrioni">Mkhedrioni</a>" ("horsemen"). The country became embroiled in a bitter <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Civil_War" title="Georgian Civil War">civil war</a>, which lasted until nearly 1995. <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a> (Soviet <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Soviet_Union)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Soviet Union)">Minister of Foreign Affairs</a> from 1985 to 1991) returned to Georgia in 1992.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Simmering disputes within two regions of Georgia, Abkhazia and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>, between local separatists and the majority Georgian populations, erupted into widespread inter-ethnic violence and wars.<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton-78">[77]</a></sup> Supported by Russia, Abkhazia and South Ossetia achieved <i>de facto</i> independence from Georgia, with Georgia retaining control only in small areas of the disputed territories.<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton-78">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Georgia,_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_(2003).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Georgia%2C_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_%282003%29.jpg/220px-Georgia%2C_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_%282003%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Georgia%2C_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_%282003%29.jpg/330px-Georgia%2C_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_%282003%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Georgia%2C_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_%282003%29.jpg/440px-Georgia%2C_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_%282003%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="916" data-file-height="687"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Georgia,_Tbilisi_-_Rose_Revolution_(2003).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Rose_Revolution" title="Rose Revolution">Rose Revolution</a>, 2003
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%931993)" title="War in Abkhazia (1992–1993)">War in Abkhazia (1992–1993)</a>, roughly 230,000 to 250,000 Georgians<sup id="cite_ref-hrwreport_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrwreport-79">[78]</a></sup> were expelled from Abkhazia by Abkhaz separatists and North Caucasian volunteers (including Chechens). Around 23,000 Georgians<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> fled South Ossetia as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2003, Shevardnadze (who won re-election in 2000) was deposed by the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Revolution" title="Rose Revolution">Rose Revolution</a>, after Georgian opposition and international monitors asserted that 2 November parliamentary elections were marred by fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> The revolution was led by <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zurab_Zhvania" title="Zurab Zhvania">Zurab Zhvania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nino_Burjanadze" title="Nino Burjanadze">Nino Burjanadze</a>, former members and leaders of Shevardnadze's ruling party. Mikheil Saakashvili was elected as President of Georgia in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the Rose Revolution, a series of reforms were launched to strengthen the country's military and economic capabilities. The new government's efforts to reassert Georgian authority in the southwestern autonomous republic of <a href="/wiki/Ajaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Ajaria">Ajaria</a> led to a major <a href="/wiki/Ajaria_Crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ajaria Crisis">crisis</a> early in 2004.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>These events, along with accusations of Georgian involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Chechen_War" title="Second Chechen War">Second Chechen War</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> resulted in a severe deterioration of <a href="/wiki/Georgia-Russia_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgia-Russia relations">relations with Russia</a>, fuelled also by Russia's open assistance and support to the two secessionist areas. Despite these increasingly difficult relations, in May 2005 Georgia and Russia reached a bilateral agreement<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> by which Russian military bases (dating back to the Soviet era) in <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">Batumi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Akhalkalaki" title="Akhalkalaki">Akhalkalaki</a> were withdrawn. Russia withdrew all personnel and equipment from these sites by December 2007<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> while failing to withdraw from the <a href="/wiki/Gudauta" title="Gudauta">Gudauta</a> base in Abkhazia, which it was required to vacate after the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Adapted_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe_Treaty" title="Adapted Conventional Armed Forces in Europe Treaty">Adapted Conventional Armed Forces in Europe Treaty</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1999_Istanbul_summit" title="1999 Istanbul summit">1999 Istanbul summit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Russo.E2.80.93Georgian_War_and_since"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russo–Georgian_War_and_since">Russo–Georgian War and since</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russo%E2%80%93Georgian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo–Georgian War">Russo–Georgian War</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia</a>
      </div>

           <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48">
