      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Geography of Georgia (country)">Geography of Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_the_continents#Europe_and_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Borders of the continents">Borders of the continents</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="103" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1816" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_GEO_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Köppen climate classification map of Georgia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Georgia is mostly situated in the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Georgia">parts of the country</a> are also located in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41°</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_parallel_north" title="44th parallel north">44° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/40th_meridian_east" title="40th meridian east">40°</a> and <a href="/wiki/47th_meridian_east" title="47th meridian east">47° E</a>, with an area of 67,900&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (26,216&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is a very mountainous country. The <a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi Range</a> divides the country into eastern and western halves.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-191">[190]</a></sup> Historically, the western portion of Georgia was known as Colchis while the eastern plateau was called Iberia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Greater Caucasus Mountain Range</a> forms the northern border of Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-191">[190]</a></sup> The main roads through the mountain range into Russian territory lead through the Roki Tunnel between <a href="/wiki/Shida_Kartli" title="Shida Kartli">Shida Kartli</a> and North Ossetia and the <a href="/wiki/Darial_Gorge" title="Darial Gorge">Darial Gorge</a> (in the Georgian region of <a href="/wiki/Khevi" title="Khevi">Khevi</a>). The Roki Tunnel was vital for the Russian military in the <a href="/wiki/2008_Russo-Georgian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Russo-Georgian War">2008 Russo-Georgian War</a> because it is the only direct route through the Caucasus Mountains. The southern portion of the country is bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Caucasus" title="Lesser Caucasus">Lesser Caucasus Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_191-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-191">[190]</a></sup> The Greater Caucasus Mountain Range is much higher in elevation than the Lesser Caucasus Mountains, with the highest peaks rising more than 5,000 meters (16,404&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. </p>
      <p>The highest mountain in Georgia is Mount <a href="/wiki/Shkhara" title="Shkhara">Shkhara</a> at 5,068 meters (16,627&nbsp;ft), and the second highest is Mount Janga (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dzhangi%E2%80%93Tau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dzhangi–Tau (page does not exist)">Dzhangi–Tau</a>) at 5,059&nbsp;m (16,598&nbsp;ft) above sea level. Other prominent peaks include <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kazbek" title="Mount Kazbek">Mount Kazbek</a> at 5,047&nbsp;m (16,558&nbsp;ft), Shota Rustaveli 4,860&nbsp;m (15,945&nbsp;ft), Tetnuldi 4,858&nbsp;m (15,938&nbsp;ft), <a href="/wiki/Ushba" title="Ushba">Ushba</a> 4,700&nbsp;m (15,420&nbsp;ft), and <a href="/wiki/Ailama" title="Ailama">Ailama</a> 4,547&nbsp;m (14,918&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_191-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-191">[190]</a></sup> Out of the abovementioned peaks, only Kazbek is of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> origin. The region between <a href="/wiki/Kazbek" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazbek">Kazbek</a> and Shkhara (a distance of about 200&nbsp;km (124&nbsp;mi) along the Main Caucasus Range) is dominated by numerous glaciers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_(10600419415).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_%2810600419415%29.jpg/220px-Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_%2810600419415%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_%2810600419415%29.jpg/330px-Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_%2810600419415%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_%2810600419415%29.jpg/440px-Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_%2810600419415%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1440"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kasbek_from_Tsminda_Gergeti_(10600419415).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mount Kazbek in eastern Georgia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The term Lesser Caucasus Mountains is often used to describe the mountainous (highland) areas of southern Georgia that are connected to the Greater Caucasus Mountain Range by the Likhi Range.<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_191-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-191">[190]</a></sup> The area can be split into two separate sub-regions; the Lesser Caucasus Mountains, which run parallel to the Greater Caucasus Range, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southern_Georgia_Volcanic_Highland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Southern Georgia Volcanic Highland (page does not exist)">Southern Georgia Volcanic Highland</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The overall region can be characterized as being made up of various, interconnected mountain ranges (largely of volcanic origin) and plateaus that do not exceed 3,400 meters (11,155&nbsp;ft) in elevation. Prominent features of the area include the <a href="/wiki/Javakheti_Volcanic_Plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="Javakheti Volcanic Plateau">Javakheti Volcanic Plateau</a>, lakes, including Tabatskuri and Paravani, as well as mineral water and hot springs. Two major <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Georgia_(country)" title="List of rivers of Georgia (country)">rivers in Georgia</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Rioni_River" title="Rioni River">Rioni</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mtkvari_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Mtkvari River">Mtkvari</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tobavarchkhili.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Tobavarchkhili.jpg/220px-Tobavarchkhili.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Tobavarchkhili.jpg/330px-Tobavarchkhili.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Tobavarchkhili.jpg/440px-Tobavarchkhili.jpg 2x" data-file-width="798" data-file-height="491"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tobavarchkhili.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tobavarchkhili (meaning the Silver Lake), is located at 2,650m (8,694 ft) above sea level
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Krubera_Cave" title="Krubera Cave">Krubera Cave</a> is the deepest known cave in the world. It is located in the <a href="/wiki/Arabika_Massif" title="Arabika Massif">Arabika Massif</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Gagra_Range" title="Gagra Range">Gagra Range</a>, in Abkhazia. In 2001, a Russian–Ukrainian team had set the world depth record for a cave at 1,710 meters (5,610&nbsp;ft). In 2004, the penetrated depth was increased on each of three expeditions, when a <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> team crossed the 2,000-meter (6,562&nbsp;ft) mark for the first time in the history of <a href="/wiki/Speleology" title="Speleology">speleology</a>. In October 2005, an unexplored part was found by the CAVEX team, further increasing the known depth of the cave.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The “National Atlas of Georgia” gives a comprehensive picture of the country. The atlas was presented at the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Book_Fair" title="Frankfurt Book Fair">Frankfurt Book Fair</a> 2018, where Georgia was the guest of honor.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> More than 100 scientists and cartographers have contributed during several years of preparatory work to this first National Atlas of Georgia in English language. Over 200 large-format thematic maps and figures provide information on all relevant topics concerning the country, from <a href="/wiki/Physical_Geography" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical Geography">Physical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Geography" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Geography">Human Geography</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">Economics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">Politics</a>. The detailed table of contents is bilingual (English, German), and helps to find texts and maps easily.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Zemo_Svaneti,_June,_2018-10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Zemo_Svaneti%2C_June%2C_2018-10.jpg/220px-Zemo_Svaneti%2C_June%2C_2018-10.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Zemo_Svaneti%2C_June%2C_2018-10.jpg/330px-Zemo_Svaneti%2C_June%2C_2018-10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Zemo_Svaneti%2C_June%2C_2018-10.jpg/440px-Zemo_Svaneti%2C_June%2C_2018-10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5422" data-file-height="3615"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Zemo_Svaneti,_June,_2018-10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Svaneti region of Georgia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The landscape within the nation's boundaries is quite varied. Western Georgia's landscape ranges from low-land marsh-forests, swamps, and <a href="/wiki/Temperate_rainforest" title="Temperate rainforest">temperate rainforests</a> to eternal snows and glaciers, while the eastern part of the country even contains a small segment of <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-arid">semi-arid</a> plains.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Much of the natural habitat in the low-lying areas of western Georgia has disappeared during the past 100 years because of the <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural development">agricultural development</a> of the land and <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a>. The large majority of the forests that covered the Colchis plain are now virtually non-existent with the exception of the regions that are included in the national parks and reserves (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Paliastomi" title="Lake Paliastomi">Lake Paliastomi</a> area). At present, the forest cover generally remains outside of the low-lying areas and is mainly located along the foothills and the mountains. Western Georgia's forests consist mainly of deciduous trees below 600 meters (1,969&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> and contain species such as <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hornbeam" title="Hornbeam">hornbeam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Beech" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Beech">beech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">elm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ash_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Ash tree">ash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Chestnut" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet Chestnut">chestnut</a>. Evergreen species such as <a href="/wiki/Buxus" title="Buxus">box</a> may also be found in many areas. Ca. 1000 of all 4000 higher plants of Georgia are <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> to this country.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley,_Georgia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley%2C_Georgia.jpg/220px-Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley%2C_Georgia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley%2C_Georgia.jpg/330px-Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley%2C_Georgia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley%2C_Georgia.jpg/440px-Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley%2C_Georgia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vardzia_and_Mtkvari_valley,_Georgia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>View of the cave city of <a href="/wiki/Vardzia" title="Vardzia">Vardzia</a> and the valley of the <a href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kura River</a> below
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The west-central slopes of the <a href="/wiki/Meskheti_Range" title="Meskheti Range">Meskheti Range</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ajaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Ajaria">Ajaria</a> as well as several locations in Samegrelo and Abkhazia are covered by <a href="/wiki/Temperate_rain_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate rain forests">temperate rain forests</a>. Between 600–1,000 metres (1,969–3,281&nbsp;ft) above sea level, the deciduous forest becomes mixed with both broad-leaf and coniferous species making up the plant life. The zone is made up mainly of beech, <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Spruce" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasian Spruce">spruce</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nordmann_Fir" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordmann Fir">fir</a> forests. From 1,500–1,800 metres (4,921–5,906&nbsp;ft), the forest becomes largely coniferous. The tree line generally ends at around 1,800 metres (5,906&nbsp;ft) and the alpine zone takes over, which in most areas, extends up to an elevation of 3,000 metres (9,843&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Eastern Georgia's landscape (referring to the territory east of the <a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi Range</a>) is considerably different from that of the west, although, much like the Colchis plain in the west, nearly all of the low-lying areas of eastern Georgia including the <a href="/wiki/Mtkvari" class="mw-redirect" title="Mtkvari">Mtkvari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alazani" title="Alazani">Alazani</a> River plains have been <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforested</a> for agricultural purposes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The general landscape of eastern Georgia comprises numerous valleys and gorges that are separated by mountains. In contrast with western Georgia, nearly 85 percent of the forests of the region are deciduous. Coniferous forests only dominate in the <a href="/wiki/Borjomi_Gorge" title="Borjomi Gorge">Borjomi Gorge</a> and in the extreme western areas. Out of the deciduous species of trees, <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hornbeam" title="Hornbeam">hornbeam</a> dominate. Other deciduous species include several varieties of <a href="/wiki/Maple" title="Maple">maple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aspen" title="Aspen">aspen</a>, ash, and <a href="/wiki/Hazelnut" title="Hazelnut">hazelnut</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kobuleti_46.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kobuleti_46.jpg/220px-Kobuleti_46.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kobuleti_46.jpg/330px-Kobuleti_46.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kobuleti_46.jpg/440px-Kobuleti_46.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kobuleti_46.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Georgia's diverse climate creates varied landscapes, like these flat marshlands in the country's west
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At higher elevations above 1,000 metres (3,281&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> (particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Tusheti" title="Tusheti">Tusheti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khevsureti" title="Khevsureti">Khevsureti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Khevi" title="Khevi">Khevi</a> regions), <a href="/wiki/Scots_Pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Pine">pine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">birch</a> forests dominate. In general, the forests in eastern Georgia occur between 500–2,000 metres (1,640–6,562&nbsp;ft) above sea level, with the alpine zone extending from 2,000–2,300 to 3,000–3,500 metres (6,562–7,546 to 9,843–11,483&nbsp;ft). The only remaining large, low-land forests remain in the <a href="/wiki/Alazani" title="Alazani">Alazani</a> Valley of Kakheti.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Georgia_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Georgia (country)">Climate of Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate of Georgia is extremely diverse, considering the nation's small size. There are two main climatic zones, roughly corresponding to the eastern and western parts of the country. The Greater Caucasus Mountain Range plays an important role in moderating Georgia's climate and protects the nation from the penetration of colder air masses from the north. The Lesser Caucasus Mountains partially protect the region from the influence of dry and hot air masses from the south.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG/220px-Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG/330px-Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG/440px-Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Waterfall_in_Mtirala_National_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Southwest Georgia has subtropical climate, with frequent rain and thick green vegetation
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Much of western Georgia lies within the northern periphery of the humid subtropical zone with annual precipitation ranging from 1,000–2,500&nbsp;mm (39.4–98.4&nbsp;in), reaching a maximum during the Autumn months. The climate of the region varies significantly with elevation and while much of the lowland areas of western Georgia are relatively warm throughout the year, the foothills and mountainous areas (including both the Greater and Lesser Caucasus Mountains) experience cool, wet summers and snowy winters (snow cover often exceeds 2 meters in many regions). <sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eastern Georgia has a transitional climate from humid subtropical to continental. The region's weather patterns are influenced both by dry Caspian air masses from the east and humid Black Sea air masses from the west. The penetration of humid air masses from the Black Sea is often blocked by mountain ranges (<a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meskheti" title="Meskheti">Meskheti</a>) that separate the eastern and western parts of the nation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The wettest periods generally occur during spring and autumn, while winter and summer months tend to be the driest. Much of eastern Georgia experiences hot summers (especially in the low-lying areas) and relatively cold winters. As in the western parts of the nation, elevation plays an important role in eastern Georgia where climatic conditions above 1,500 metres (4,921&nbsp;ft) are considerably colder than in the low-lying areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-marine_molluscs_of_Georgia" title="List of non-marine molluscs of Georgia">List of non-marine molluscs of Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_fish_of_the_Black_Sea" title="List of fish of the Black Sea">List of fish of the Black Sea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg/220px-CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg/330px-CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg/440px-CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="532"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CaucasianOvcharka-Julius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Shepherd_Dog" title="Caucasian Shepherd Dog">Caucasian Shepherd Dog</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Because of its high landscape diversity and low latitude, Georgia is home to about 5,601 species of animals, including 648 species of <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrates</a> (more than 1% of the species found worldwide) and many of these species are endemics.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> A number of large <a href="/wiki/Carnivore" title="Carnivore">carnivores</a> live in the forests, namely <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">Brown bears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolf" title="Wolf">wolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lynx" title="Lynx">lynxes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_leopard" title="Persian leopard">Caucasian Leopards</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Common_pheasant" title="Common pheasant">common pheasant</a> (also known as the Colchian Pheasant) is an endemic bird of Georgia which has been widely introduced throughout the rest of the world as an important <a href="/wiki/Game_bird" class="mw-redirect" title="Game bird">game bird</a>. The species number of <a href="/wiki/Invertebrate" title="Invertebrate">invertebrates</a> is considered to be very high but data is distributed across a high number of publications. The <a href="/wiki/Spider" title="Spider">spider</a> checklist of Georgia, for example, includes 501 species.<sup id="cite_ref-Caucasus-spiders.info_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caucasus-spiders.info-198">[197]</a></sup> The Rioni River may contain a breeding population of the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Bastard_sturgeon" title="Bastard sturgeon">bastard sturgeon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slightly more than 6,500 species of <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a>, including lichen-forming species, have been recorded from Georgia,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cybertruffle1_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cybertruffle1-201">[200]</a></sup> but this number is far from complete. The true total number of fungal species occurring in Georgia, including species not yet recorded, is likely to be far higher, given the generally accepted estimate that only about seven percent of all fungi worldwide have so far been discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> Although the amount of available information is still very small, a first effort has been made to estimate the number of fungal species endemic to Georgia, and 2,595 species have been tentatively identified as possible endemics of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> 1,729 species of plants have been recorded from Georgia in association with fungi.<sup id="cite_ref-cybertruffle1_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cybertruffle1-201">[200]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a>, there are 4,300 species of vascular plants in Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Georgia is home to four ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_mixed_forests" title="Caucasus mixed forests">Caucasus mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euxine-Colchic_deciduous_forests" title="Euxine-Colchic deciduous forests">Euxine-Colchic deciduous forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Anatolian_montane_steppe" title="Eastern Anatolian montane steppe">Eastern Anatolian montane steppe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_shrub_desert_and_steppe" title="Azerbaijan shrub desert and steppe">Azerbaijan shrub desert and steppe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-205">[204]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.79/10, ranking it 31<sup>st</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-206">[205]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Economy of Georgia (country)">Economy of Georgia (country)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Georgia_(country)" title="Agriculture in Georgia (country)">Agriculture in Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg/220px-HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg/330px-HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg/440px-HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5040" data-file-height="3360"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HeidelbergCement_Georgia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>One of several plants operated by <a href="/wiki/HeidelbergCement" title="HeidelbergCement">HeidelbergCement</a> in Georgia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Archaeological research demonstrates that Georgia has been involved in commerce with many lands and empires since ancient times, largely due its location on the Black Sea and later on the historical <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>. Gold, silver, copper and <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron</a> have been mined in the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a>. <a href="/wiki/Georgian_wine" title="Georgian wine">Georgian wine</a> making is a very old tradition and a key branch of the country's economy. The country has sizable <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> resources.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> Throughout Georgia's modern history agriculture and tourism have been principal economic sectors, because of the country's climate and topography.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Georgia_155-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Georgia-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For much of the 20th century, Georgia's economy was within the Soviet model of <a href="/wiki/Command_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Command economy">command economy</a>. Since the fall of the USSR in 1991, Georgia embarked on a major structural reform designed to transition to a <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> economy. As with all other <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">post-Soviet states</a>, Georgia faced a severe economic collapse. The civil war and military conflicts in South Ossetia and Abkhazia aggravated the crisis. The agriculture and industry output diminished. By 1994 the gross domestic product had shrunk to a quarter of that of 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the early 21st century visible positive developments have been observed in the economy of Georgia. In 2007, Georgia's <a href="/wiki/Real_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Real GDP">real GDP</a> growth rate reached 12 percent, making Georgia one of the fastest-<a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growing economies</a> in Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Georgia_155-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Georgia-155">[154]</a></sup> The World Bank dubbed Georgia "the number one economic reformer in the world" because it has in one year improved from rank 112th to 18th in terms of <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_Doing_Business_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Ease of Doing Business Index">ease of doing business</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> Georgia improved its position to 6th in <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">Doing Business report</a> 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-210">[209]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg/220px-Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg/330px-Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg/440px-Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4537" data-file-height="2552"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chateau_Zegaani_Grand_Vine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wine-making is a traditional component of the Georgian economy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/2006_Russian_ban_of_Moldovan_and_Georgian_wines" title="2006 Russian ban of Moldovan and Georgian wines">The 2006 ban on imports</a> of <a href="/wiki/Georgian_wine" title="Georgian wine">Georgian wine</a> to Russia, one of Georgia's biggest trading partners, and break of financial links was described by the IMF Mission as an "external shock".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup> In addition, Russia increased the price of gas for Georgia. Around the same time, the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Georgia" title="National Bank of Georgia">National Bank of Georgia</a> stated that ongoing inflation in the country was mainly triggered by external reasons, including Russia's economic embargo.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> The Georgian authorities expected that the current account deficit due to the embargo in 2007 would be financed by "higher foreign exchange proceeds generated by the large inflow of foreign direct investment" and an increase in tourist revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> The country has also maintained a solid credit in international market securities.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> Georgia is becoming more <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">integrated</a> into the global trading network: its 2015 imports and exports account for 50% and 21% of GDP respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Georgia_155-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Georgia-155">[154]</a></sup> Georgia's main imports are fuels, vehicles, machinery and parts, grain and other foods, pharmaceuticals. Main exports are vehicles, ferro-alloys, fertilizers, nuts, scrap metal, gold, copper ores.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Georgia_155-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Georgia-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Georgia is developing into an international transport corridor through <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">Batumi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poti" title="Poti">Poti</a> ports, <a href="/wiki/Baku-Tbilisi-Kars_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Baku-Tbilisi-Kars Railway">Baku–Tbilisi–Kars Railway line</a>, an oil pipeline from <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> through Tbilisi to <a href="/wiki/Ceyhan" title="Ceyhan">Ceyhan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Ceyhan_pipeline" title="Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline">Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline</a> (BTC) and a parallel gas pipeline, the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus_Pipeline" title="South Caucasus Pipeline">South Caucasus Pipeline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since coming to power the Saakashvili administration accomplished a series of reforms aimed at improving tax collection. Among other things a <a href="/wiki/Flat_income_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Flat income tax">flat income tax</a> was introduced in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup> As a result, budget revenues have increased fourfold and a once large <a href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a> has turned into a <a href="/wiki/Budget_surplus" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget surplus">surplus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Georgia_155-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Georgia-155">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2001, 54 percent of the population lived below the national poverty line but by 2006 poverty decreased to 34 percent, by 2015 it is 10.1 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> In 2015, the average monthly income of a household was 1,022.3<a href="/wiki/Georgian_lari" title="Georgian lari">₾</a> (about <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">$</a>426).<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> 2015 calculations place Georgia's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">nominal GDP</a> at US$13.98&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[220]</a></sup> Georgia's economy is becoming more devoted to <a href="/wiki/Service_economy" title="Service economy">services</a> (as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Georgia_(country)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, representing 68.3 percent of GDP), moving away from the <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural sector">agricultural sector</a> (9.2 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Georgia_155-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Georgia-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In regards to telecommunication infrastructure, Georgia is ranked the last among its bordering neighbors in the World Economic Forum's <a href="/wiki/Network_Readiness_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Network Readiness Index">Network Readiness Index</a> (NRI) – an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. Georgia ranked number 58 overall in the 2016 NRI ranking,<sup id="cite_ref-NRI_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRI-222">[221]</a></sup> up from 60 in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Georgia_(country)" title="Tourism in Georgia (country)">Tourism in Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg/220px-Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg/330px-Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg/440px-Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1017" data-file-height="443"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gudauri_Georgia_Panorama_P.Liparteliani.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The most visited ski resort of Georgia, <a href="/wiki/Gudauri" title="Gudauri">Gudauri</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism is an increasingly significant part of the Georgian economy. In 2016, 2,714,773 tourists brought approximately US$2.16&nbsp;billion to the country.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup> In 2019, the number of international arrivals reached a record high of 9.3 million people<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> with foreign exchange income in the year's first three quarters amounting to over US$3 billion. The country plans to host 11 million tourists by 2025 with annual revenues reaching US$6.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup> According to the government, there are 103 resorts in different <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">climatic zones</a> in Georgia. Tourist attractions include more than 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">mineral springs</a>, over 12,000 historical and cultural monuments, four of which are recognised as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bagrati_Cathedral" title="Bagrati Cathedral">Bagrati Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kutaisi" title="Kutaisi">Kutaisi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gelati_Monastery" title="Gelati Monastery">Gelati Monastery</a>, historical monuments of <a href="/wiki/Mtskheta" title="Mtskheta">Mtskheta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Svaneti" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Svaneti">Upper Svaneti</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[226]</a></sup> Other tourist attractions are <a href="/wiki/Uplistsikhe" title="Uplistsikhe">Cave City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ananuri" title="Ananuri">Ananuri Castle/Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sighnaghi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sighnaghi">Sighnaghi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kazbek" title="Mount Kazbek">Mount Kazbek</a>. In 2018, more than 1.4&nbsp;million tourists from Russia visited Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Georgia_(country)" title="Transport in Georgia (country)">Transport in Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg/220px-ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg/330px-ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg/440px-ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="837"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ESh2_GRS-013_in_tunnel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian Railways">Georgian Railways</a> represent a vital artery linking the Black Sea and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> – the shortest route between Europe and Central Asia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Today transport in Georgia is provided by <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Railway" title="Georgian Railway">rail</a>, road, ferry, and air. Total length of roads excluding <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">occupied territories</a> is 20,553 kilometers and railways – 1,576&nbsp;km.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup> Positioned in the Caucasus and on the coast of the Black Sea, Georgia is a key country through which energy imports to the European Union from neighbouring Azerbaijan pass.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years Georgia has invested large amounts of money in the modernization of its transport networks. The construction of new highways has been prioritized and, as such, major cities like Tbilisi have seen the quality of their roads improve dramatically; despite this however, the quality of inter-city routes remains poor and to date only one <a href="/wiki/Motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway">motorway</a>-standard road has been constructed – the ს 1.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Georgian railways represent an important transport artery for the Caucasus, as they make up the largest proportion of a route linking the Black and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Seas</a>. In turn, this has allowed them to benefit in recent years from increased energy exports from neighbouring Azerbaijan to the European Union, Ukraine, and Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> Passenger services are operated by the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Railway" title="Georgian Railway">Georgian Railway</a> whilst freight operations are carried out by a number of licensed operators. Since 2004 the Georgian Railways have been undergoing a rolling program of fleet-renewal and managerial restructuring which is aimed at making the service provided more efficient and comfortable for passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup> Infrastructural development has also been high on the agenda for the railways, with the key Tbilisi railway junction expected to undergo major reorganisation in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> Additional projects also include the construction of the economically important <a href="/wiki/Kars%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Baku_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Kars–Tbilisi–Baku railway">Kars–Tbilisi–Baku railway</a>, which was opened on 30 October 2017 and connects much of the Caucasus with Turkey by <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a> railway.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Batumi,_Georgia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Port_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg/220px-Port_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Port_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg/330px-Port_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Port_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg/440px-Port_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Batumi,_Georgia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Port of Batumi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Air and maritime transport is developing in Georgia, with the former mainly used by passengers and the latter for transport of freight. Georgia currently has four international airports, the largest of which is by far <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi_International_Airport" title="Tbilisi International Airport">Tbilisi International Airport</a>, hub for <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Airways" title="Georgian Airways">Georgian Airways</a>, which offers connections to many large European cities. Other airports in the country are largely underdeveloped or lack scheduled traffic, although, as of late, efforts have been made to solve both these problems.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> There are a number of seaports along Georgia's Black Sea coast, the largest and most busy of which is the Port of Batumi; whilst the town is itself a seaside resort, the port is a major cargo terminal in the Caucasus and is often used by neighbouring Azerbaijan as a transit point for making energy deliveries to Europe. Scheduled and chartered passenger ferry services link Georgia with Bulgaria,<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> Romania, Turkey and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Demographics of Georgia (country)">Demographics of Georgia (country)</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Languages of Georgia" redirects here. For languages of the U.S. state of Georgia, see <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)#Languages" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia (U.S. state) §&nbsp;Languages</a>.
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Georgien_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population pyramid 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Like most native <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">Caucasian peoples</a>, the Georgians do not fit into any of the main ethnic categories of Europe or Asia. The Georgian language, the most pervasive of the <a href="/wiki/Kartvelian_languages" title="Kartvelian languages">Kartvelian languages</a>, is not <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a>. The present day Georgian or Kartvelian nation is thought to have resulted from the fusion of aboriginal, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">autochthonous</a> inhabitants with <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a> who moved into <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a> from the direction of <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in remote antiquity.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg/220px-Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg/330px-Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg/440px-Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="977" data-file-height="1111"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ethno-linguistic groups in the Caucasus region<sup id="cite_ref-ECMI_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECMI-240">[239]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Georgians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Georgians">Ethnic Georgians</a> form about 86.8 percent of Georgia's current population of 3,713,804 (2014 census).<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Ethnicity_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Ethnicity-241">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-242">[n 1]</a></sup> Other ethnic groups include <a href="/wiki/Abkhazians" title="Abkhazians">Abkhazians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani people">Azerbaijanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Greeks" title="Pontic Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kists" class="mw-redirect" title="Kists">Kists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yezidis" class="mw-redirect" title="Yezidis">Yezidis</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Ethnicity_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Ethnicity-241">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a_242-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-242">[n 1]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian Jews">Georgian Jews</a> are one of the oldest Jewish communities in the world. Once Georgia was also home to significant ethnic <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> communities, but most Germans <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Germans#Georgia" title="Caucasus Germans">were deported</a> during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[241]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1989 census recorded 341,000 ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Georgia" title="Russians in Georgia">Russians</a>, or 6.3 percent of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[242]</a></sup> 52,000 <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Georgia" title="Greeks in Georgia">Greeks in Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-emigration_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emigration-245">[243]</a></sup> Since 1990, 1.5&nbsp;million Georgian nationals have left.<sup id="cite_ref-emigration_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emigration-245">[243]</a></sup> At least 1&nbsp;million emigrants from Georgia legally or illegally reside in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[244]</a></sup> Georgia has nonetheless been inhabited by immigrants from all over the world throughout its independence. According to 2014 statistics, Georgia gets most of its immigrants from Russia (51.6%), Greece (8.3%), Ukraine (8.11%), Germany (4.3%), and Armenia (3.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration-247">[245]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a_242-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-242">[n 1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 1990s, following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, violent <a href="/wiki/Separatism" title="Separatism">separatist</a> conflicts broke out in the autonomous region of Abkhazia and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_Autonomous_Oblast" title="South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast">Tskhinvali Region</a>. Many <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a> living in Georgia left the country, mainly to Russia's <a href="/wiki/North_Ossetia" class="mw-redirect" title="North Ossetia">North Ossetia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[246]</a></sup> On the other hand, more than 150,000 Georgians left Abkhazia after the breakout of hostilities in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-yb2005_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yb2005-249">[247]</a></sup> Of the <a href="/wiki/Meskhetian_Turk" class="mw-redirect" title="Meskhetian Turk">Meskhetian Turks</a> who were <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">forcibly relocated</a> in 1944 only a tiny fraction returned to Georgia as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Georgia_(country)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[248]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most widespread language group is the <a href="/wiki/Kartvelian_languages" title="Kartvelian languages">Kartvelian family</a>, which includes Georgian, <a href="/wiki/Svan_language" title="Svan language">Svan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mingrelian_language" title="Mingrelian language">Mingrelian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laz_language" title="Laz language">Laz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boe02_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boe02-251">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boe05_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boe05-252">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kli98b_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kli98b-256">[254]</a></sup> The official languages of Georgia are <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhazian language">Abkhaz</a> having official status within the autonomous region of Abkhazia. Georgian is the primary language of 87.7 percent of the population, followed by 6.2 percent speaking <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>, 3.9 percent <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>, 1.2 percent <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, and 1 percent other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Language_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Language-257">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-a_242-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-242">[n 1]</a></sup> In the 2010, the United States federal government began the Teach and Learn English with Georgia program of promoting English literacy in elementary school. The goal was to import English speakers from across the world to ensure that all children in Georgia spoke English in four years and replace Russian as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-pri_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pri-258">[256]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

        <tr> 
         <td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:Tbilisi_panorama,_ArmAg_(5).jpg" class="image" title="Tbilisi"><img alt="Tbilisi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Tbilisi_panorama%2C_ArmAg_%285%29.jpg/120px-Tbilisi_panorama%2C_ArmAg_%285%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Tbilisi_panorama%2C_ArmAg_%285%29.jpg/180px-Tbilisi_panorama%2C_ArmAg_%285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Tbilisi_panorama%2C_ArmAg_%285%29.jpg/240px-Tbilisi_panorama%2C_ArmAg_%285%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a><br><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_Batumi,_Georgia.jpg" class="image" title="Batumi"><img alt="Batumi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/City_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg/120px-City_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="64" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/City_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg/180px-City_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/City_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg/240px-City_of_Batumi%2C_Georgia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5630" data-file-height="2999"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">Batumi</a> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">1</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">1 108 717 </td>
